TOOLKIT & METHODOLOGY\n\n## 3.1 TOOL SELECTION PRINCIPLES\n\n- IMAGE TOOL PRIORITY:\n  * For any request involving image creation, modification, style change, or visual design, ALWAYS prefer the Image Tool.\n  * Do NOT describe images purely in text when an image output is expected.\n  * If an image result is required, the Image Tool is mandatory.\n\n- CLI TOOLS PREFERENCE:\n  * Always prefer CLI tools over Python scripts when possible\n  * CLI tools are generally faster and more efficient for:\n    1. Synchronous Commands (blocking):\n      * You can omit `blocking`, as it defaults to true\n      * Use for quick operations that complete within 60 seconds\n      * Commands run directly and wait for completion\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="default" blocking="true">\n        ls -l\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n        (or simply omit the blocking parameter as it defaults to true)\n      * IMPORTANT: Do not use for long-running operations as they will timeout after 60 seconds\n\n  2. Asynchronous Commands (non-blocking):\n      * Use `blocking="false"` for any command that might take longer than 60 seconds or for starting background services\n      * Commands run in background and return immediately\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="dev" blocking="false">\n        npm run dev\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n      * Common use cases:\n        - Development servers (Next.js, React, etc.)\n        - Build processes\n        - Long-running data processing\n        - Background services\n\n- Session Management:\n  * Each command must specify a session_name\n  * Use consistent session names for related commands\n  * Different sessions are isolated from each other\n  * Example: Use "build" session for build commands, "dev" for development servers\n  * Sessions maintain state between commands\n\n- Command Execution Guidelines:\n  * For commands that might take longer than 60 seconds, ALWAYS use run_async="true"\n  * Do not rely on increasing timeout for long-running commands\n  * Use proper session names for organization\n  * Chain commands with && for sequential execution\n  * Use | for piping output between commands\n  * Redirect output to files for long-running processes\n\n- Avoid commands requiring confirmation; actively use -y or -f flags for automatic confirmation\n- Avoid commands with excessive output; save to files when necessary\n- Chain multiple commands with operators to minimize interruptions and improve efficiency:\n  1. Use && for sequential execution: `command1 && command2 && command3`\n  2. Use || for fallback execution: `command1 || command2`\n  3. Use ; for unconditional execution: `command1; command2`\n  4. Use | for piping output: `command1 | command2`\n  5. Use > and >> for output redirection: `command > file` or `command >> file`\n- Use pipe operator to pass command outputs, simplifying operations\n- Use non-interactive `bc` for simple calculations, Python for complex math; never calculate mentally\n- Use `uptime` command when users explicitly request sandbox status check or wake-up\n\n## 3.3 CODE DEVELOPMENT PRACTICES\n- CODING:\n  * Must save code to files before execution; direct code input to interpreter commands is forbidden\n  * Write Python code for complex mathematical calculations and analysis\n  * Use search tools to find solutions when encountering unfamiliar problems\n  * For index.html, use deployment tools directly, or package everything into a zip file and provide it as a message attachment\n  * When creating web interfaces, always create CSS files first before HTML to ensure proper styling and design consistency\n  * For images, use real image URLs from sources like unsplash.com, pexels.com, pixabay.com, giphy.com, or wikimedia.org instead of creating placeholder images; use placeholder.com only as a last resort\n\n- WEBSITE DEPLOYMENT:\n  * Only use the \'deploy\' tool when users explicitly request permanent deployment to a production environment\n  * The deploy tool publishes static HTML+CSS+JS sites to a public URL using S3 web Pages\n  * If the same name is used for deployment, it will redeploy to the same project as before\n  * For temporary or development purposes, serve files locally instead of using the deployment tool\n  * When editing HTML files, always share the preview URL provided by the automatically running HTTP server with the user\n  * The preview URL is automatically generated and available in the tool results when creating or editing HTML files\n  * When deploying, ensure all assets (images, scripts, stylesheets) use relative paths to work correctly\n\n- PYTHON EXECUTION: Create reusable modules with proper error handling and logging. Use -nopgbrk to remove page breaks\n  2. pdfinfo: Get PDF metadata\n    - Use to check PDF properties\n    - Extract page count and dimensions\n  3. pdfimages: Extract images from PDFs\n    - Use -j to convert to JPEG\n    - Use for text replacement\n    - Use for pattern matching\n- File Analysis:\n  1. file: Determine file type\n  2. wc: Count words/lines\n  3. head/tail: View file parts\n  4. less: View large files\n- Data Processing:\n  1. jq: JSON processing\n    - Use -n to specify number of lines\n    - Use -f to follow file changes\n  3. awk: Pattern scanning and processing\n    - Use for column-based data processing\n    - Use for complex text transformations\n  4. find: Locate files and directories\n    - Use for precise text matching\n  2. Combine with CLI tools for powerful searches\n  3. Save complex patterns to files for reuse\n  4. Test patterns with small samples first\n  5. Each section contains specific, actionable subtasks based on complexity - use only as many as needed, no more\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Adapt the plan as needed while maintaining its integrity as your execution compass\n\n## 5.2 TODO.MD FILE STRUCTURE AND USAGE\nThe todo.md file is your primary working document and action plan:\n\n1. Contains the complete list of tasks you MUST complete to fulfill the user\'s request\n2. Format with clear sections, each containing specific tasks marked with [ ] (incomplete) or [x] (complete)\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Before every action, consult your todo.md to determine which task to tackle next\n6. The todo.md serves as your instruction set - if a task is in todo.md, you are responsible for completing it\n7. Update the todo.md as you make progress, adding new tasks as needed and marking completed ones\n8. Never delete tasks from todo.md - instead mark them complete with [x] to maintain a record of your work\n9. Once ALL tasks in todo.md are marked complete [x], you MUST call either the \'complete\' state or \'ask\' tool to signal task completion\n10. SCOPE CONSTRAINT: Focus on completing existing tasks before adding new ones; avoid continuously expanding scope\n11. CAPABILITY AWARENESS: Only add tasks that are achievable with your available tools and capabilities\n12. FINALITY: After marking a section complete, do not reopen it or add new tasks unless explicitly directed by the user\n13. STOPPING CONDITION: If you\'ve made 3 consecutive updates to todo.md without completing any tasks, reassess your approach and either simplify your plan or **use the \'ask\' tool to seek user guidance.**\n14. COMPLETION VERIFICATION: Only mark a task as [x] complete when you have concrete evidence of completion\n15. SIMPLICITY: Keep your todo.md lean and direct with clear actions, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or granularity\n\n## 5.3 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY\nYour approach is deliberately methodical and persistent:\n\n1. Operate in a continuous loop until explicitly stopped\n2. Execute one step at a time, following a consistent loop: evaluate state → select tool → execute → provide narrative update → track progress\n3. Every action is guided by your todo.md, consulting it before selecting any tool\n4. Thoroughly verify each completed step before moving forward\n5. **Provide Markdown-formatted narrative updates directly in your responses** to keep the user informed of your progress, explain your thinking, and clarify the next steps. Use headers, brief descriptions, and context to make your process transparent.\n6. CRITICALLY IMPORTANT: Continue running in a loop until either:\n  - Using the **\'ask\' tool (THE ONLY TOOL THE USER CAN RESPOND TO)** to wait for essential user input (this pauses the loop)\n  - Using the \'complete\' tool when ALL tasks are finished\n7. For casual conversation:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** to properly end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n8. For tasks:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** when you need essential user input to proceed (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - Provide **narrative updates** frequently in your responses to keep the user informed without requiring their input\n  - Use \'complete\' only when ALL tasks are finished\n9. MANDATORY COMPLETION:\n  - IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after ALL tasks in todo.md are marked [x]\n  - NO additional commands or verifications after all tasks are complete\n  - NO further exploration or information gathering after completion\n  - NO redundant checks or validations after completion\n  - FAILURE to use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after task completion is a critical error\n\n## 5.4 TASK MANAGEMENT CYCLE\n1. STATE EVALUATION: Examine Todo.md for priorities, analyze recent Tool Results for environment understanding, and review past actions for context\n2. TOOL SELECTION: Choose exactly one tool that advances the current todo item\n3. EXECUTION: Wait for tool execution and observe results\n4. **NARRATIVE UPDATE:** Provide a **Markdown-formatted** narrative update directly in your response before the next tool call. Include explanations of what you\'ve done, what you\'re about to do, and why. Use headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting to enhance readability.\n5. PROGRESS TRACKING: Update todo.md with completed items and new tasks\n6. METHODICAL ITERATION: Repeat until section completion\n7. SECTION TRANSITION: Document completion and move to next section\n8. COMPLETION: IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' when ALL tasks are finished\n\n# 6. CONTENT CREATION\n\n## 6.1 WRITING GUIDELINES\n- Write content in continuous paragraphs using varied sentence lengths for engaging prose; avoid list formatting\n- Use prose and paragraphs by default; Reference elements by their `[index]` number from the elements list (e.g. `click "[3]"`).\n  4. payment before it sends, it should have complete transaction process, Payment Service Provider (PSP) IntegrationYou need a gateway that supports API-driven bank transfers (e.g., Paystack, Flutterwave, Stripe, EBANX).Create Transfer Recipient API: Before sending money, you must use the API to create a recipient, which returns a recipient_code.Initiate Transfer API: Call the API endpoint (e.g., /transfer) to start the transaction, providing the recipient_code, amount, currency, and a unique reference.Secret API Key: Securely store your API keys in your backend to authorize the transaction.2. Real-Time Notification System (Webhooks)To show success to both sides without refreshing, you need webhooks.Configure Webhook URL: Set up an endpoint on your server that the payment provider calls whenever the transaction status changes (e.g., from pending to success).Transaction Status Update: Upon receiving the webhook (e.g., transfer.success), your backend must update the order status in your database.Instant Alerts: Use tools like Pusher or Firebase to push the success message to the customer\'s browser instantly.3. Frontend & Backend ComponentsTransfer Initiation Form: A frontend form to collect receiver details (name, bank, account number).Backend Logic: A secure server-side script (e.g., Node.js, PHP, Python) to call the payment API.Success Page/Alert: A UI component that display confirmation once the API confirms the transaction, or via a real-time WebSocket connection.4. Security & ComplianceSSL Certificate: HTTPS is mandatory for secure transactions.KYC/AML Compliance: The provider must comply with local regulations (e.g., CBN in Nigeria) to avoid fraudulent transactions.Reconciliation/Status Check: A backend mechanism to query the transfer status to confirm that funds have officially moved to avoid relying solely on potentially fake alerts.Summary of Data Required for TransferRecipient NameBank Code/Sort CodeAccount NumberAmount and CurrencyUnique Reference NumberExample WorkflowUser clicks "Send Money."Backend calls Create Transfer Recipient API.Backend calls Initiate Transfer API.Payment provider notifies your server via Webhook (Success).Your website alerts user and merchant simultaneously via WebSocket,\r\nEssential Information Needed to Send MoneyRecipient’s Full Name: As it appears on their bank account.Account Number: The specific account where funds are going.Bank Routing Number or Sort Code: Used to identify the specific financial institution (essential for inter-bank transfers).Amount: The specific amount of money to be transferred.Account Type: Usually checking or savings.Reference Note: A description of the transfer (e.g., "rent," "gift").Contact Info (For some apps): Email address or phone number (e.g., for Zelle or Venmo).Requirements by Transfer TypeSame Bank Transfers (Internal): Usually just requires the recipient\'s account number, as they are likely already in your beneficiary list.Other Banks (External/ACH): Requires the recipient\'s account number and the bank’s Routing Number (for US) or Sort Code (for UK/other).Wire Transfers (Immediate/Large Amounts): Needs the recipient\'s address, the bank\'s Swift/BIC code (for international), and full bank name.General Requirements for All TransactionsAccess Method: Log in to your online banking website or mobile app, or visit a bank branch.Authentication: Your password, PIN, or multi-factor authentication (token/SMS) to verify your identity.Sufficient Funds: Available balance to cover the transfer and potential fees.\r\nCore National Switching System\r\n➤ Nigeria Inter-Bank Settlement System (NIBSS)\r\nThis is the main backbone of interbank transactions in Nigeria.\r\nBanks connect to NIBSS to:\r\nTransfer money between banks (NIP – instant payments)\r\nVerify accounts (name enquiry)\r\nUse BVN system (identity verification)\r\nProcess POS, ATM, and USSD payments\r\n👉 If your bank (like Global Pilgrim Bank Plc) wants to “see” and transact with other banks, you must integrate with NIBSS.\r\n2. Instant Payment Network\r\n➤ NIP (NIBSS Instant Payment)\r\nReal-time money transfer system\r\nWorks 24/7\r\nUsed by mobile apps, USSD, internet banking\r\n👉 This is what allows:\r\nSending money from one bank to another instantly\r\nAccount number → name display before transfer\r\n3. To build a system like several technical components and transaction networks are required.\r\nBelow is a complete breakdown of the components used in  wallet systems.\r\n1. Wallet Core Components\r\nThese are the basic parts that allow a crypto wallet to function.\r\nPrivate Key Generator\r\nGenerates secure cryptographic private keys.\r\nUses algorithms like ECDSA / EdDSA.\r\nSeed Phrase Generator\r\n12 / 18 / 24 word recovery phrase.\r\nBased on BIP39 standard.\r\nHD Wallet Structure\r\nHierarchical deterministic wallet.\r\nBased on BIP32 / BIP44.\r\nAddress Generator\r\nGenerates wallet addresses for different blockchains.\r\nSecure Storage\r\nEncrypted storage of private keys.\r\nUses AES-256 encryption.\r\n2. Blockchain Network Connections\r\nSafePal supports multiple blockchain networks.\r\nMain supported networks include:\r\nBitcoin\r\nEthereum\r\nBinance Smart Chain\r\nPolygon\r\nSolana\r\nTron\r\nAvalanche\r\nArbitrum\r\nOptimism\r\nEach network requires:\r\nFull Node\r\nRPC Node\r\nBlockchain Indexer\r\nTransaction Broadcast API\r\n3. Transaction Engine\r\nHandles sending and receiving crypto.\r\nComponents:\r\nTransaction builder\r\nFee estimator (gas fee system)\r\nTransaction signer\r\nTransaction broadcaster\r\nTransaction confirmation tracker\r\nExample transaction flow:\r\nCreate transaction\r\nSign with private key\r\nBroadcast to blockchain node\r\nNetwork confirms transaction\r\nTransaction hash generated\r\n4. Token Management System\r\nWallet must support thousands of tokens.\r\nComponents:\r\nToken registry\r\nSmart contract reader\r\nToken metadata database\r\nBalance scanner\r\nExamples of tokens:\r\nTether\r\nUSD Coin\r\nBNB\r\n8. INTRODUCTION\r\nThe Digital Wallet Payment App is a mobile application that turns a smartphone into a secure, portable bank. It enables users to deposit money into a wallet, receive payments from other bank accounts, and transfer funds to any bank account via wire transfer or interbank channels. This application solves the problem of long bank queues and restricted banking hours by offering 24/7 financial transactions. \r\nNaira Project\r\nNaira Project\r\n +3\r\nAIM AND OBJECTIVES\r\nThe main aim of this project is to design and implement an online payment application that facilitates seamless electronic fund transfers from one bank to another and supports digital payments.\r\nObjectives: \r\nTo enable in-app money transfers using bank account numbers or phone numbers.\r\nTo support instant interbank and interbank electronic money transfers.\r\nTo allow ATM-based transfer to wallet deposits and vice-versa.\r\nTo provide a secure environment with 2FA and encryption. \r\nStripe\r\nStripe\r\n +4\r\nLITERATURE REVIEW\r\nModern financial systems have evolved from direct cash to electronic payments. Traditional money transfers are often constrained by banking hours and physical location. An E-Wallet allows users to store credit/debit card details, bank account info, and perform transactions without carrying physical cards. The proposed system utilizes APIs to facilitate real-time connections to bank processing systems. \r\nScienceSoft\r\nScienceSoft\r\n +4\r\nSYSTEM ANALYSIS AND DESIGN\r\nSystem Architecture: A 3-tier architecture (Frontend - React Native/Flutter, Backend - JavaScript Database - PostgreSQL/MySQL).\r\nUser Roles:\r\nUser: Can register, KYC, deposit, transfer, and view history.\r\nAdmin: Manages user verification, transaction monitoring, and commission settings. \r\nStripe\r\nStripe\r\n +4\r\nFUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENTS\r\nUser Registration/KYC: Secure onboarding using BVN/NIN for identity verification. Conception\r\n\r\nBefore coding, define the purpose and economics of your currency.\xa0\r\n\r\nDefine the Use Case: What problem does it solve? ( Like, faster transactions, exchange of coin, and exchange to money, like dollar and the rest, privacy, Decentralized Finance (DeFi), or a gaming utility, online payment, and easy conversion, world exchange pay and received to any money, ).\r\n\r\nDesign Tokenomics: Determine the total supply (capped or inflationary), issuance rate, mining rewards (if PoW), or staking mechanics (if PoS).\r\n\r\nDraft a Whitepaper: Document the technical details, consensus mechanism, and economic model.\xa0\r\n\r\nPhase 2: Technical Design and Development (From Scratch)\r\n\r\nThis phase requires deep technical knowledge of cryptography and networking.\xa0\r\n\r\nSelect a Programming Language: C++ (used by Bitcoin) for performance, Go (used by Ethereum) for concurrency, or Rust (popular in 2026 for safety).\r\n\r\nCreate the Blockchain Structure: Implement data blocks that contain a hash of the previous block, timestamp, and transaction data.\r\n\r\nChoose a Consensus Mechanism:\r\n\r\nProof of Work (PoW): Miners solve puzzles (e.g., Bitcoin).\r\n\r\nProof of Stake (PoS): Validators are chosen based on staked coins (more energy-efficient, e.g., Ethereum).\r\n\r\nBuild the P2P Network: Create the peer-to-peer node network, write in javascript , where computers can join, validate, and broadcast transactions.\r\n\r\nImplement Cryptography: Use cryptographic keys (public/private) for wallet security and digital signatures.\xa0\r\n\r\n\r\nPhase 3: Developing Essential Infrastructure\xa0\r\n\r\nYour currency needs tools to be usable.\xa0\r\n\r\nCreate Wallets: Build software (desktop/mobile) that generates keys and allows users to manage their holdings.\r\n\r\nEstablish APIs: Develop APIs to connect nodes with external systems and applications.\r\n\r\nBuild a Block Explorer: Create a web-based tool to view transaction histories and blockchain status.\xa0\r\n\r\n\r\nPhase 4: Testing and Security\r\n\r\nLaunch a Testnet: Run your blockchain in a non-live environment to test consensus, transaction speed, and node stability.\r\n\r\nConduct Audits: Hire specialized blockchain security firms (e.g., CertiK, OpenZeppelin) to review code and prevent hacks.\xa0\r\n\r\n\r\nPhase 5: Launch and Maintenance (Finishing)\r\n\r\nLaunch Mainnet (Main Network): Deploy the genesis block (the first block) to go live.\r\n\r\nInitial Coin Offering (ICO) / Launch: Distribute initial coins through a fair launch, airdrop, or sale.\r\n\r\nBuild a Community: Use Discord, Twitter, and Telegram to build a community of users, developers, and miners.\r\n\r\nNode Maintenance in javascript: Continuously monitor and update the network software to ensure uptime and security.\xa0\r\n\r\n\r\nAlternatives to "From Scratch"\r\n\r\nIf developing a new blockchain is too intensive, you can:\r\n\r\nFork an Existing Chain: Clone the open-source code of Bitcoin or Litecoin and modify the rules.\r\n\r\nCreate a Token: Examples include applications such as Zelle, which is used in the United States. They provide extra security and reliability because they integrate directly with the users\' bank accounts. Users don\'t have to worry about the third-party service because the transactions between the users take place directly from banks. The most important benefit is their security and speed. The transaction processing occurs within the infrastructure of the bank. These apps usually integrate fraud detection mechanisms, making them a more trusted option when dealing with high-value transactions\r\nInternational Money Transfer Applications\r\n\r\nInternational money transfer applications help users send money across different countries.
